<div id="review_2675936102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2675936102" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2675936102?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42943098-the-wicked-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2675936102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5968837523809313259">4.5/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/05/07/the-wicked-king-the-folk-of-the-air-2-by-holly-black/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605949254i/30407018._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='380' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <i>
    <b>“Because, for a moment, when I was at my worst, I felt powerful, and most of the time, I felt powerless.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>What that ending was, I have no idea, but I turned from crying out of pure candid joy to crying out of frustration. <br/><br/>With this book, the whole <i>
  <b>The Folk of the Air</b>
</i> trilogy goes from 0 to 100 really quick. I could feel an increase of the pacing in the first book (which was packed with action), a pace that was a bit slowed </span>
  <span id="freeText5968837523809313259" style="display:none">4.5/5 ⭐<br><br><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/05/07/the-wicked-king-the-folk-of-the-air-2-by-holly-black/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605949254i/30407018._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="380" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <i>
    <b>“Because, for a moment, when I was at my worst, I felt powerful, and most of the time, I felt powerless.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>What that ending was, I have no idea, but I turned from crying out of pure candid joy to crying out of frustration. <br><br>With this book, the whole <i>
  <b>The Folk of the Air</b>
</i> trilogy goes from 0 to 100 really quick. I could feel an increase of the pacing in the first book (which was packed with action), a pace that was a bit slowed down in this one, but it picked up towards the end.<br><br>This book has fantastic action.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“A king is a living symbol, a beating heart, a star upon which Elfhame’s future is written.”</b>
  </i>
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584648033i/29132963._SY540_.jpg" width="254" height="358" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>I started to dislike various characters of this book more than initially.<br><br>Taryn was never one of my favourites, but her part in this book makes her look less in my eyes. Even though she seems disturbed herself, she is too naïve and easily manipulated by her absolute desires of normalcy. And she’s stubborn about them too.<br><br>Vivi seemed totally great in the first book. I actually came to love her. But in this one, she’s definitely changed. Some of her certain actions do not represent her as they should and so, she’s no less amongst my own personal list of favourites of the book.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508784473ra/24254146.gif" width="250" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Whom I really came to love though are the Roach and the Bomb. I thought at first that they were okay, but after this, OMG, I love them. Especially the Bomb. Like, she’s really cool and knows how to play everything off. And also SHE’S A MASTER OF EXPLOSIVES so she has a popping personality indeed. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“The disturbing thing about Cardan is how well he plays the fool to disguise his own cleverness.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>I’ve already said this but I am going to repeat myself: I AM IN LOVE WITH CARDAN.<br><br>He’s still <b>“The boy who still hoped he might be loved”</b>. I love you, Cardan boy, don’t you worry that pretty head of yours. <br><br>As the action goes on, I just can’t help but fall in love with him with every chapter. He’s just…such an amazing character that sometimes I feel like he’s the only one who’s been blessed with character depth (even though the characters' own emotional profiles seem to deepen in this book more than in the first one). Cardan just gets better and better and he surprised me with his cunning and wisdom more than once.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584648510i/29132996._SX540_.jpg" width="240" height="190" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>
    <b>“He is ridiculously beautiful as ever, mouth soft, lips slightly parted. Lashes so long that when his eyes are closed they rest against his cheek.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>I can’t get over this portrait of Cardan exposed to us by Jude, who carefully examines the High King’s every move. She’s obviously and furiously in love with him, but aren’t we all? (At least some of us admit it though, unlike others *ahem* Jude) <br><br>Their relationship is still weird. I have to say it. But I think that even this weirdness has its own uniqueness, its own interesting trait that I can’t let go of, but I can’t condemn either. It’s something wickedly interesting going on with this pair and I am kind of liking it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I hate you so much that sometimes I can't think of anything else.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>After this book, I still like Jude.<br><br>Again, she’s a bit annoying sometimes, she is impulsive and tends to be rational until the verge of irrationality. But I am still fond of her. And I kind of understand everything she does because she’s just a mortal girl playing at high life. Even though she’s playing a dangerous and foreign game, she still doesn’t have to know all the moves. I am the type of person figuring things out while on my way of doing them so I am completely understanding Jude and all her discontinuity in life.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1584648033ra/29132964.gif" width="322" height="185" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>I am a bit still not okay with the last 20 pages of the book though. It really made me very emotional and hurt and even though I hated it, I also loved the twist of it.<br><br>It was such a good read and all I got left after reading this second book is the feeling of more. By this point, I think it is a bit hard not to love this whole plot. It’s truly fantastic.<br><br>________________________________________<br><br><b>Also see:</b> <br>#1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2675936211" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince</a> (⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐)<br>#3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2763398749?type=review#rating_277176610" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Nothing</a> (⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐)<br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/9e69b327-767c-4cdc-95f0-3f7fa08d794e_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5968837523809313259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3374696725" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3374696725" />
    <a title="Mary S. R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r"><img alt="Mary S. R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597037601p2/75831724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3374696725?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary S. R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary S. R." href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r">Mary S. R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/51208952-the-wicked-king">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">you, if you harbour a secret dark corner in your soul</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=faves">faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3374696725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14722421277975440774"><b>I hate this book.</b><br/><br/>I hate it so much I can’t stop thinking about it. I hate it enough to wanna make 100 accounts to rate it one star over & over again.<br/><br/>But I won’t, not because that’s immoral but because <b>there can’t be hate unless there is love.</b> There can’t be loss unless there is need. There can’t be hurt unless there is care.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“I hate you,” I say, the words coming out like a caress. I say it again, over and over. A litany. An enchantment. A ward against what I really feel.</i>
</blockquote><br/>So really, it’s my own</span>
  <span id="freeText14722421277975440774" style="display:none"><b>I hate this book.</b><br><br>I hate it so much I can’t stop thinking about it. I hate it enough to wanna make 100 accounts to rate it one star over &amp; over again.<br><br>But I won’t, not because that’s immoral but because <b>there can’t be hate unless there is love.</b> There can’t be loss unless there is need. There can’t be hurt unless there is care.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I hate you,” I say, the words coming out like a caress. I say it again, over and over. A litany. An enchantment. A ward against what I really feel.</i>
</blockquote><br>So really, it’s my own damn fault. <b>I all but handed Holly Black a gilded dagger, turned my back, and begged her to <i>please please stab me right in the feels</i>, going so far as to give her directions to the place just south of my hopes and slightly north of my dreams.</b><br><br>I am Jude and this book is my <i>Wicked King</i>.<br><br>And there is no better way, absolutely none, to convey how it feels to read its every page, every brush of ink, every curve and crease, than to quote the book itself: <i>It has all the sinister pleasure of sneaking out of the house, all the revolting satisfaction of stealing. It reminds me of the moment before I slammed a blade through my hand, amazed at my own capacity for self-betrayal.</i> (Please do excuse me for stealing lines—I do so because I am an inadequate piece of human soul and incapable of competing with the Faerie Queen who wrote this pure trove of gems).<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Power is much easier to acquire than it is to hold on to.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I have said it before, and I’ll say it again: People don’t paint this series as it truly is. <b><i>The Folk of the Air</i> is not a light, romantic fairytale, however addictive; it’s a dark and deadly one—less a page-turner and more a temptress. It’s about tricks and snares, games and intrigue and pain and, above all else, power. Infectious, greedy, alluring <i>power</i>.</b><br><br>And that, all of that, weaves itself through every nook, around every thread of the books. It hugs Jude’s curves and flies from her lips, slides along Cardan’s tail and between his clever clasp. It wraps its hungry grasp around the characters, bathing, entombing, suffocating. And it, quite gloriously, circles the dynamics and bonds, twisting and blurring the lines of love and hate, want and fear, until it is one with its every angle, dip, and chip. I guess it makes sense some would mistake one for the other.<br><br>Isak Danielson’s song <i>Power</i> (<i>which you can find on my <a href="https://open.spotify.com/playlist/2pIObm4BIDL2NJFfVKyXzg" rel="nofollow noopener">book playlist</a></i>) is <i>The Wicked King</i> incarnate and why oh why didn’t I listen when people told me NOT to finish it before an exam and went ahead to do just that? Sigh, I’m a fool, yes, but a fool for Jude and Cardan. And that never ceases to be an honour.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Things are always super dramatic around here,” Vivi tells Heather. “Epic. Everyone acts as though they just stepped out of a murder ballad.”</i>
</blockquote><br>As I called this book a <i>pure trove of gems</i>, I will proceed to refer to the treasures as the four most precious gemstones:<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600013671i/30101619.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>
  <u>Black Diamond: <i>Jude Duarte</i></u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Once upon a time, there was a human girl stolen away by faeries, and because of that, she swore to destroy them.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I will fight every single person who dares call my Jude annoying or unbearable and anything else in the thesaurus for those adjectives. She is the definition of a brilliant badass queen and I am willing to rip throats to prove it. Metaphorically, of course.<br><br>In <i>The Cruel Prince</i> she evolved from the girl who wanted to impress and fit in and fight for honour, to a ruthless, power-hungry, scheming star, and in this sequel her shine multiplies a thousandfold; so I suggest you all shield your eyes before you go blind from her magnificence. <b>Exploring her hatred of vulnerability, her need for control, and her insistence on relentlessly pushing and <i>pushing</i> herself both physically and mentally to the brink of collapse until she’s achieved perfection and utter independence, made me relate to her on a level that bordered on discomfort</b>, if comfort really had any meaning (<i>at least to me</i>) and I wasn’t such a self-absorbed bastard.<br><br>The sheer <i>will</i>. That, right there, is my most adored trait in human or faerie, reality or fiction.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You’re unwinding yourself like a spool. What happens when there’s no more thread?”<br>“Then I spin more.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Anger or fear? Fear or anger?</b> Jude would argue anger (<i>unsurprisingly, that is, her being a furious hurricane and all</i>) and I happen to agree. Both are overwhelming emotions that can drown and paralyse and turn one into a fool, while both can also motivate and embolden and turn one into a champion. However, there is a certain strand of arrogance interwoven with amger that fear happens to lack. And, you all know me, I would pick anger over fear any day.<br><br>So I can do nothing less than shout my love for her from the rooftops, no mountains, as <b>Jude takes the hurt and weakness the Folk carved into her flesh and bone, adds it to the stew of her desire to be magic like them mixed with her obsessive knowledge of their rules and their ways and the music of their strings as they are pulled and plucked, and sprinkles it with a formidable amount of pleasure from the power and the dance and determination to learn and excel, watching it all bubble and burn.</b> She is certainly my favourite cook, because she is better at being worse than them. Never, ever underestimate my little murderer’s strength, her skill at strategy, and her capacity for cruelty.<br><br>Lastly, I want to raise a glass to the question Holly raises with this book: <i>Is it good, or bad, for a ruler to contain those cutting, cunning impulses?</i> Answer that as you will.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600013671i/30101619.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>
  <u>Cat’s Eye Emerald: <i>Cardan Greenbriar</i></u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Have you never heard that virtue is its own reward?” Cardan says pleasantly. “That’s because there’s no other reward in it.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Ahhhh, I am in love with this wicked king (<i>while wanting to strangle him to death and back, ofc</i>) and I’m not even sorry.<br><br>I stand by my point in my review of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555997072" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince</a>
</i> that his most important difference from most wicked charming boys (<i>or girls</i>) in books, is his <i>absolute lack of ambition.</i> Hell, that’s also the main difference between him and Jude. <b>This small (<i>perhaps inconsequential to most fans</i>) detail is so ridiculously highlighted for me because it makes him endearing and unique and helplessly adorable, adding to his irresistible charm as he languishes on life, and <i>why am I swooning right now ugh</i>.</b><br><br><i>The Wicked King</i> is undoubtedly the best installment in this trilogy and one of the reasons for that is Cardan’s beautiful, heart-stopping growth as a character. He goes from a person commited to, as Jude would put it, “being a layabout who does none of the real work of governance,” to finding himself, his resolve, mettle, fight—whatever you want to call it—because of how his feeling of powerlessness and fear trickle away, drip by drip, as he no longer has someone to inflame (<i>Jude excluded</i>). And, mostly, because of Jude pushing him unwittingly.<br><br>He learns to <i>own</i> it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“The three of you have one solution to every problem. Murder. No key fits every lock.” Cardan gives us all a stern look, holding up a long-fingered hand with my stolen ruby ring still on one finger. “Someone tries to betray the High King, murder. Someone gives you a harsh look, murder. Someone disrespects you, murder. Someone ruins your laundry, murder.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I could go on for two more paragraphs about why he seems to “have a singular taste for women who threaten” him and why and how a certain type of power dynamic appeals to our dear twisted fearie as it, honestly, does to most of the messed up characters in this series, but I won’t bore you anymore with my psychological talk. <b>I will just go ahead and carve a Cardan-shaped chamber deep in my cold, dark heart to trap this clever, cutting, shameless, straightforward yet playful boy and protect him at all costs.</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600013671i/30101619.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>
  <u>Burmese Ruby: <i>The Jurdan Ship</i></u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“If you’re the sickness, I suppose you can’t also be the cure.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I mean whoever wasn’t already abroad this ship should be careful because I might kindly push them overboard for being late to the party (<i>let’s ignore the fact that I was also late to the general party shhhhh</i>). <b>If book one was them warming for the match, book two is them sparring at full swing <i>and I am here for it</i>.</b> And “what is sparring but a game of strategy, played at speed?” So just as he is wary of her, bracing for her next blow while enjoying the game and trusting her completely, he is also going to land blows. Really, it’s only fair.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I have heard that for mortals, the feeling of falling in love is very like the feeling of fear. Your heart beats fast. Your senses are heightened. You grow light-headed, maybe even dizzy.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I think my second favourite aspect of their relationship (<i>after the games and sparring match</i>) is how <b>their need and attraction and glimpse of a kindred spirit morphs into denial and fury and fiery hatred as they run away from the feeling they despise lacing through their love, all while being helpless to do so.</b> Running at full speed on the tilted ground drenched with a rain of pain and desire, Cardan has already slipped. It’s Jude’s turn to do so.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Kiss me again,” he says, drunk and foolish. “Kiss me until I am sick of it.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Now, I’m going to make a confession. I was as stupefyingly petrified of their dynamic shifting as Jude was. Every step he took beyond her control, every claim he made to his own self, every fistful of power he dug up, I found myself screaming <i>no no</i> just as much as I cheered his growth. Because I understand her fear of being out of control and powerless, and do not want him to hold more power than Jude. And that fear is idiotic and unfair, because the fact that one’s power should come out of another’s powerlessness needs to give everyone pause.<br><br><b>He has capered while she schemed, it’s time for them to learn to be equals, with mutual trust even in their game of chess, having faith in the fact that their opponent and partner will <i>never land a killing blow</i>.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“For a moment,” he says, “I wondered if it wasn’t you shooting bolts at me.”<br>I make a face at him. “And what made you decide it wasn’t?”<br>He grins up at me. “They missed.”</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600013671i/30101619.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>
  <u>Violet Sapphire: <i>Rest of the Rabble</i></u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Like the ant in the fable who labors in the dirt while the grasshopper sings the summer away.”<br>“And has nothing left for winter,” I say.<br>“I need for nothing,” he says, shaking his head, mock-mournful. “I am the Corn King, after all, to be sacrificed so little Oak can take my place in the spring.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>✧ <i>Storytelling:</i></b> I might’ve read only one trilogy by <i>Holly Black</i>, but I can safely say she is one true Weaver; taking the tale by the throat, dunking it in an ocean of vocabulary and punctuations, and threading the water and words into whorls of magic and enchantment. Thank you, Holly, for weaving waves of wailing tales for us.<br><br><b>✧ <i>Worldbuilding:</i></b> No words can capture and frame my love for this mystical, fairytaleish land of exotic, quiet allure, so I’m not even gonna try.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m still your father.”<br>“You’re my father’s murderer,” I blurt out.<br>“I can be both,” Madoc says, smiling, showing those teeth.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>✧ <i>Madoc:</i></b> I could not tear my gaze away from this messed up father-daughter relationship. He, the monster who took everything from Jude, also gave her a new life, pushed her to her fullest potential (<i>even while underestimating her</i>), encouraged her fire (<i>even while beating her down</i>), was all is she had. And I lived for how thoroughly this facet of this dark tapestry, this theme of moving past and beyond the power of the person who raised you, burns throughout the book.<br>P.S. <i>Pain makes you strong</i>? Sith much?<br><br><blockquote>
<i>“Your ridiculous family might be surprised to find that not everything is solved by murder,” Locke calls after me.<br>“We </i>would<i> be surprised to find that,” I call back.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>✧ <i>Taryn the Betrayer:</i></b> I argued in my review of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3373069978" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Sisters</a>
</i> that Taryn likes the games and adventure and power play and is fierce enough to claim her own tale (<i>while being hypocritical enough to deny it</i>). And she does. But doesn’t mean she is not weak, because she is that, too. She escapes confrontation and discomfort like a sunflower constantly turning towards the sun to flee the darkness—and I’ve never much liked sunflowers. This adaptability is exactly what fascinates Locke, and this weakness is just what takes apart the trust between these two lost sisters.<br><br><b>✧ <i>Locke the F***ing Fox:</i></b> I know everyone hates and wants to kill this guy, but I can’t resist bringing him back to life after choking him for more of his playful, dangerous-but-fun fox games of backstabbing delight. *sheepish smile*<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Revenge is sweet, but ice cream is sweeter.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>✧ <i>Vivi the Humanlover:</i></b> A moment’s appreciation for mt defiant yet chill, loving yet selfish knight-at-heart.<br><br><b>✧ <i>Fala the Fool:</i></b> Putting him here because NO ONE SEEMS TO CARE FOR THIS GEM WHY. K I’mma truly shut up now bye.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600013671i/30101619.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Companions</b>
</u><br><br><b>
  <i>Book series playlist:</i>
</b> <a href="https://open.spotify.com/playlist/2pIObm4BIDL2NJFfVKyXzg" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify URL<br><br><blockquote><blockquote><blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600013671i/30101620._SY540_.jpg" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></blockquote></blockquote></blockquote></a><br><b>
  <i>Books in series:</i>
</b><br>➳ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555997072" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince</a> (The Folk of the Air, #1) ★★★★★<br>➳ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3373069978" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Sisters</a> (The Folk of the Air, #1.5) ★★★★☆<br>➳ The Wicked King (The Folk of the Air, #2) ★★★★★<br>➳ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3382713133" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Nothing</a> (The Folk of the Air, #3) ★★★★☆<br> ➳ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3391069744" rel="nofollow noopener">How the King of Elfhame Learned to Hate Stories</a> (The Folk of the Air, #3.5) ☆☆☆☆☆</span>
  <a data-text-id="14722421277975440774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2196158268" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2196158268" />
    <a title="Korrina  (OwlCrate)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37437502-korrina-owlcrate"><img alt="Korrina  (OwlCrate)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417291917p2/37437502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2196158268?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Korrina  (OwlCrate)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Korrina  (OwlCrate)" href="/user/show/37437502-korrina-owlcrate">Korrina  (OwlCrate)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2196158268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5309312596634152040">It’s a great feeling to fall in utter love with the first book in a new series, and then anticipate the sequel, and then be offered a chance to read said sequel early, and then to read this book in 24 hours and savour every bit of it. Very few series that I’ve read in my life have hooked me as much as this one. The only downside? The agonizing two year wait for the third book!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2135853984" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2135853984" />
    <a title="Cindy ✩☽♔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3222333-cindy"><img alt="Cindy ✩☽♔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605643833p2/3222333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2135853984?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy ✩☽♔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy ✩☽♔" href="/user/show/3222333-cindy">Cindy ✩☽♔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316487139" href="/book/show/40870568-the-wicked-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2135853984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer811521217473486721"><b>Power is so much easier to acquire than it is to hold on to.</b><br/><br/>I'm not sure if I should be happy or angry? <br/><br/>This book was, undoubtedly, my most anticipated book of the year. But I must confess, it did not quite live up to my expectations. That's not to say it is not a good book, it was just a tad slow for my taste. The book doesn't really pick up until about the 60% mark. After that though, things definitely get interesting. <br/><br/><u>Main Characters' Ranking:</u><br/><i>Jude = Cardan > Madoc = Vivi >> Locke >>>>>>>> Tar</i></span>
  <span id="freeText811521217473486721" style="display:none"><b>Power is so much easier to acquire than it is to hold on to.</b><br><br>I'm not sure if I should be happy or angry? <br><br>This book was, undoubtedly, my most anticipated book of the year. But I must confess, it did not quite live up to my expectations. That's not to say it is not a good book, it was just a tad slow for my taste. The book doesn't really pick up until about the 60% mark. After that though, things definitely get interesting. <br><br><u>Main Characters' Ranking:</u><br><i>Jude = Cardan &gt; Madoc = Vivi &gt;&gt; Locke &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Taryn </i><br>Previously I disliked Taryn for being weak and complicit, but now I just loathe her for being a lousy, backstabbing, sorry excuse for a sister. <br><br><b><u>The Relationships</u>:</b><br><u>Madoc &amp; Jude</u><br>Even though I know they'll never truly reconcile, some small part of me wishes they would because honestly a Madoc and Jude team-up would be epic. They would have all of Faerie bending to their will. No question. <br><br>It is clear that despite her previous betrayal Madoc does still care about Jude and wants her to join his side. <br><i>"Does our High King have any idea how good you are at running this kingdom for him?"<br>"Keep hoping he doesn't"<br>"Oh, I shall, daughter, much as I hope you will realize how much better it would be if you were to be running it for your own family."</i><br>But alas he is still who he is and any sort of personal feelings he may have fall second to his boundless ambition. <br><br><u>Jude &amp; Taryn</u><br>If this series somehow ends with Jude easily forgiving Taryn for betraying her AGAIN. I will riot!<br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=124ydzt" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1546400442ra/26847216.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br>Honestly, this is the reason I did not even bother to read The Lost Sisters. Because any amount of Taryn is too much Taryn for me. I do not care what anyone says about how she has her own way of coping or surviving in Faerie. Because the bottom line is both Jude and Taryn have suffered in this world their whole lives, but only ONE of them has betrayed the other. TARYN. Sure Jude may not have told Taryn her every plan and secret, but never once has Jude intentionally done something to harm Taryn. NOT ONCE. And just when she starts to let her sister back in, Taryn just slaps her in the face with another betrayal. <br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=nmakja" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1546489806ra/26851418.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Honestly, I am so done with this relationship. May it wither and die. <br><br><u>Jude &amp; Cardan</u><br>To put it simply this relationship is a mess. A beautiful mess, but a mess nonetheless. Because once again we're forced to watch truly deeply damaged individuals fight their obviously growing feelings for one another because they lack the fundamental key to a healthy relationship, trust. <br>On Jude's part: <br><i>...that I like him better than I've ever liked anyone and that of all the things he's ever done to me, making me like him so much is by far the most</i><br><i>...and all I want to do is walk into his arms. I want to drown my worries in his embrace. I want him to say something totally unlike himself, about things being okay. </i><br><i>Kill him before he makes you love him</i> <br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=1zvdf1v" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1536332224ra/26267554.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>On Cardan's part: <br><i>"Kiss me again, he says, drunk and foolish. "Kiss me until I am sick of it."</i><br><i>"If you're the sickness, I suppose you can't also be the cure."</i><br><i>"I wasn't kind Jude. Not to many people. Not to you. I wasn't sure if I wanted you or if I wanted you gone from my sigh so that I would stop feeling as I did, which made me even more unkind. But when you were gone-truly gone beneath the waves-I hated myself as I never have before."</i><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=awtbt1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518963907ra/25082100.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>These two have the makings of something beautifully tragic. And I suppose the ending of this book makes some people angry. Angry at Cardan. But personally, I found it fitting. A betrayal to answer a betrayal. An eye for an eye. It is the world they live in. The only way to win is to play, and it seems Cardan is finally done taking a backseat. So while I am disappointed our girl got played, I am not mad at Cardan for finally taking his life into his own hands. And that's the tea. <br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2e3oh8h" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1546490195ra/26851421.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sidenote: one running theme I found quite amusing is how often people pointed out Jude's affinity for murder.<br>For example: <br>Locke-Jude <br><i>"Your ridiculous family might be surprised to find that not everything is solved by murder."<br>"We would be surprised to find that."</i><br><br>Cardan-Jude-The Roach-The Bomb<br><i>"The three of you have one solution to every problem. Murder. No key fits every lock."<br>"Someone tries to betray the High King, murder. Someone gives you a harsh look, murder. Someone disrespects you, murder. Someone ruins your laundry, murder."</i><br><br>All-in-all this was a mighty fine read and a great book to kick off my year. <br><br>===<br>NOTE: My Headcanon came true!!!<br>Headcanon: Cardan and Jude will continue to have an unwanted, yet undeniable pull and attraction to one another. And one of those times will involve some fun with Cardan's tail. <br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=15d2849" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514994514ra/24823458.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="811521217473486721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2548674736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2548674736" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2548674736?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316310352" href="/book/show/38237340-the-wicked-king">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/69919640-sol-thebookishking">Sol ~ TheBookishKing</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=bookstagram-made-me-do-it">bookstagram-made-me-do-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2548674736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5385420736960469320"><b>CONGRATULATIONS-Goodreads Choice Awards YA Fantasy Winner!</b><br/><br/>Ok so here's the deal-<b>I wasn't crazy about The Cruel Prince.</b> <i>There, I said it.</i> The reason I'm starting this review with a seemingly negative attitude is two-fold: 1) It shows the sheer amount of growth that Black provides between the first two books in this series and 2) It shows that I'm not just blowing smoke up your ass and being pushed to give this a high rating to boost sales. <i>The Wicked King</i> was a true delight and privilege to read,</span>
  <span id="freeText5385420736960469320" style="display:none"><b>CONGRATULATIONS-Goodreads Choice Awards YA Fantasy Winner!</b><br /><br />Ok so here's the deal-<b>I wasn't crazy about The Cruel Prince.</b> <i>There, I said it.</i> The reason I'm starting this review with a seemingly negative attitude is two-fold: 1) It shows the sheer amount of growth that Black provides between the first two books in this series and 2) It shows that I'm not just blowing smoke up your ass and being pushed to give this a high rating to boost sales. <i>The Wicked King</i> was a true delight and privilege to read, my fellow bookworms, and I hope I can do it a shred of justice while discussing it here. <b>This review is 100% spoiler free!</b><br /><br />Our story begins five months after the events of <i>The Cruel Prince</i> take place, and we are immediately thrown into the narrative with dollops of those previous five months sprinkled in along the way. While I suppose it isn't ABSOLUTELY necessary, I would highly encourage you to pick up the novella <i>The Lost Sisters</i> as it gives an insightful look into Taryn's side of things during TCP (and also packs an extra emotional punch for a particular twist included at the end of this novel). There are a lot of moving parts to this middle installment, and some may seem fairly unrelated in the beginning, but by the end they all come together nicely for a whopper of an ending.<br /><br />The aspect that stands out most to me regarding <i>The Wicked King</i> is the tremendous amount of character growth accomplished in just a short amount of time (and page count). Where TCP featured fairly typical/stereotypical characters for YA fantasy and only really connected me to the story near the ending when the twists started coming, TWK really fleshed out the deepest, darkest desires and fears of our cast and put them on display for their fellow peers. I don't want to say too much, but by the end of this novel I felt such a connection to many of the characters that I didn't really care about the previous go around.<br /><br /><b>AND THAT ENDING?!</b> It's been quite some time since I've been so taken aback <i>multiple times</i> in the final 25% of a novel. It was waves of twists, turns, and heart breaking revelations. The ending is enough to make you dig out a tub of ice cream and wallow in your emotional breakdown for days. I have some thoughts on how I feel the next book could go, but after the ending here, Ms. Black has shown the reader that she owns these folks and she'll do with them as she pleases. <i>Muahahahaha</i> <br /><br />I think I'll stop here and just let you experience it for yourself, but if you haven't pre-ordered this one yet, what are you waiting for? Despite having read this one already, I have still managed to pre-order the regular hardcover and the BN special edition.... because obviously, my shelves need this blessing in their life. &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="5385420736960469320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2519986163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2519986163" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2519986163?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316487139" href="/book/show/40870568-the-wicked-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2519986163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16089924549086762367"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2073418506' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Cruel Prince</a> ★★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2519986163' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wicked King</a> ★★★★★ <br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2267451762' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen of Nothing</a> ???<br/><br/><i>After the shocking turn of events that finished off The Cruel Prince, Jude is fighting with everything she’s got to keep the kingdom of Elfhame from falling to pieces under its new rulers. Unfortunately for Jude, not only is a war brewing in the Undersea, but the court is full of traitors—and a few of them might be in her own home.</i></blockquote><br/>I loved <i>The Cruel Prince,</i> but I wasn’t <b>one hundred percent sold</b> on certain factors—yet, fr</span>
  <span id="freeText16089924549086762367" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2073418506" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince</a> ★★★★★<br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2519986163" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wicked King</a> ★★★★★ <br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2267451762" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Nothing</a> ???<br /><br /><i>After the shocking turn of events that finished off The Cruel Prince, Jude is fighting with everything she’s got to keep the kingdom of Elfhame from falling to pieces under its new rulers. Unfortunately for Jude, not only is a war brewing in the Undersea, but the court is full of traitors—and a few of them might be in her own home.</i></blockquote><br />I loved <i>The Cruel Prince,</i> but I wasn’t <b>one hundred percent sold</b> on certain factors—yet, from the moment I finished reading it, I’ve been saying the same thing: “Everything I struggled with in book 1, I <i>know</i> will be better in book 2.” Was I right? Let me put it this way: you know the “second book slump” people always refer to in trilogies? NOT AN ISSUE HERE. Everything that <i>The Cruel Prince</i> does well, <i>The Wicked King</i> does <b>
  <i>PERFECTLY.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>→ L I K E S :</u>
</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> I’ve wanted this and feared it, and now that it’s happening, I don’t know how I will ever want anything else.</b>
</blockquote><br />First, without spoiling anything, let’s get this out of the way: <b>the weird, hateful, hot-and-cold relationship between Jude and Cardan</b> progresses <i>flawlessly</i>, and by that I mean I cheered, I raged, I cried, I swooned, I blushed, I raged some more… it’s beautiful. I’ve never seen enemies-to-lovers done quite like this, because at all times, they’re kind of… <i>both?</i> Let me tell you, the phrase “I hate you” has never been this sexy.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>My body has acclimated, and now it craves what it should revile.</b>
</blockquote><br />And Jude, my gods, <b>JUDE.</b> She is a <b>masterpiece.</b> I love her so much. She’s coldhearted, cruel, murderous, backstabbing, and a total antihero in all the best ways. She’s earned herself a permanent place on my favorite “terrifying leading ladies I love” list. She’s also so clever and strong; despite being betrayed at every possible turn, she manages to constantly work things to her favor—or, at the very least, to take someone else down with her as brilliantly as possible.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“The last room Cardan occupied caught fire. Let me rephrase. It caught fire because <i>he lit it on fire.</i>”</b>
</blockquote><br />Also, Holly Black’s writing is just legitimately so <i>funny</i>, I can’t even describe. It’s incredibly rare that a book makes me laugh out loud, but I cracked up over so many weird and ridiculous moments—usually pertaining to Cardan’s absolute lack of any common decency and/or sense.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> Angry was better than being scared. Better than remembering she was a mortal among monsters.</b>
</blockquote><br />Finally, of course, there’s the world. I adore Holly’s commitment to writing a version of Faerieland that follows legitimate fae lore, and just like in the first book, that authenticity comes through effortlessly. All the world-building and political complexity she offered in the first book paid off so well in this sequel.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>→ D I S L I K E S :</u>
</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>That I like him better than I’ve ever liked anyone and that of all the things he’s ever done to me, making me like him so much is by far the worst.</b>
</blockquote><br />Literally the <i>
  <b>only</b>
</i> thing I didn’t like about <i>The Wicked King</i> is the fact that I have over a year to wait before finding out what the hell is going on with this terrible, infuriating, <i>priceless</i> cliffhanger ending. I mean, take the way Jude feels about Cardan, and that’s basically me towards Holly Black right now, except replace the “burning carnal desire” with “desperate need to find out how it all ends, right NOW”.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>→ F I N A L THOUGHTS :</u>
</b><br /><br />In all seriousness, <i>The Wicked King</i> was literal perfection in my eyes and I would not change a single thing. I flew through it, I loved every page, I highlighted so many quotes I can’t even fit a quarter of them in this review, and I don’t know if I have ever felt so simultaneously torn and <i>obsessed</i> with any pairing as I am over Jude and Cardan.<br /><br />Oh, and one more thing: <b>TARYN STILL AIN’T SHIT.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>→ RECOMMENDING TO… :</u>
</b><br /><br />Everyone. Just… literally everyone.<br /><br /><i>All quotes come from an advance copy and may not match the final release. Thank you so much to a very sweet (and unnamed) friend for loaning me their ARC!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16089924549086762367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2321686174" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2321686174" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2321686174?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471408038" href="/book/show/42428253-the-wicked-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favourite-covers">favourite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series-to-complete">series-to-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2321686174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14685591615810448418">I genuinely cannot believe this book was basically about what happens when you let a drunk furry be king<br/><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“Once upon a time, there was a human girl stolen away by faeries, and because of that, she swore to destroy them.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>YOOO Holly Black did it again! The politics !! The characters !!! The angst !!! AND THAT ENDING. I enjoyed this even more than book one - it was so dark, twisted, with even more political intrigue, betrayal and scheming. Part two especially was incredible, and all leading up t</span>
  <span id="freeText14685591615810448418" style="display:none">I genuinely cannot believe this book was basically about what happens when you let a drunk furry be king<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Once upon a time, there was a human girl stolen away by faeries, and because of that, she swore to destroy them.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />YOOO Holly Black did it again! The politics !! The characters !!! The angst !!! AND THAT ENDING. I enjoyed this even more than book one - it was so dark, twisted, with even more political intrigue, betrayal and scheming. Part two especially was incredible, and all leading up to that ENDING. It packed the biggest punch, and I am so, so, so freakin excited to see where she goes and what she does next with book two. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Kiss me again,” he says, drunk and foolish. “Kiss me until I am sick of it.” <br /></blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The Wicked King opens a few weeks after the ending of The Cruel Prince. Almost immediately we are thrown back into the action and politics, and catch up with all the main characters and how what happened at the end of TCP is affecting them. I don't want to talk too much about plot due to spoilers but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2240056694?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">read my review of the cruel prince if you haven't read that book yet. </a><br /><br />The pacing of this book was much better than the first one. I immediately was drawn right back into the world and the politics. These books are so immersive and I think that is what makes them so fun. You really get caught up in the characters world and care SO MUCH about what is happening to them - and I think being sucked into a whole new world and forgetting your own is one of the best things about fantasy. This series does that for me so well, so even if there is other things I don't love as much in here, I really have to give it points for the pure joy that this escapism gives me. <br /><br />Just like The Cruel Prince, the politics in this also kept me right on my toes. I really love how Holly Black plays with perspective in these books, and uses off-page action to conceal the motivations and plans of various characters. She is really good at building mystery - giving you just enough to get intrigued but not enough to guess everything that going to happen. But I also am SO GRATEFUL her reveals make sense - that feeling when everything suddenly clicks into place and you wonder how you missed it all along is the best. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I hate you,” I breathe into his mouth. “I hate you so much that sometimes I can’t think of anything else.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>AND with that quote ! Lets talk characters -- </b><br /><br />✨<b>
  <u>Jude</u>
</b> ACTUAL love of my life. She is too powerful, extremely scary in a hot way and its my kink. I really think Jude is such a GREAT main character. I've said this about her before but I adore how ruthless and cold she is - the fact she borders on villain (and would look like the villain if this wasn't from her POV) is so interesting and I just really enjoy following her. The Wicked King really exposes more of her insecurities and flaws which I liked, the development has been good and I CANNOT WAIT TO SEE WHAT SHE DOES IN QUEEN OF NOTHING FUCK IT UP QUEEN I ADORE YOU. <br /><br />✨<b>
  <u>Cardan</u>
</b> thats ! my ! man !! At this point in my YA reading career I'm used to falling for the actual dickhead white boy and I was got again. Anyways, I don't really like him but his character is so fun. He had so much development in this, and a lot more page time which was nice. His and Jude's scenes were easily the highlight of the book and those scenes above all really sucked me in. I will say - I kinda wasn't loving some of his backstory. But I'm going to get more into that in the romance section so stay tuned. <br /><br />✨<b>
  <u>Taryn</u>
</b> I'm just gonna say it .... yall hate on her WAY too much and she doesn't deserve it. I actually really like Taryn. She is a literal juxtaposition of Jude - I mean they're idential twins, raised in the same home in the same situation, two sides of the same coin who chose different paths but could have easily been the other. Do you know how much I LIVE for that shit. Taryn is basically Jude - like if this was from Taryn's point of view, Jude would look like what Taryn looks like to us and I find that INTERESTING AS FUCK. So yeah, her roll in the series is so intriguing to me and of all the characters in Queen of Nothing, I'm actually MOST excited to see what she does. <br /><br />✨<b>
  <u>Everyone else</u>
</b> Honestly, I don't have many thoughts on Madoc except I wish he wasn't there anymore. The Roach and the Bomb as Jude's weird murder found family was cute. Locke can choke. Nicasia intrigued me quite a lot in this and I hope we get more on her history with Cardan - is it bad I kinda ship her and Cardan a lot ?? Vivi was a MESS and everything she did was bad. Orlagh should have been in it more. Balekin is the most annoying little shit. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Someone tries to betray the High King, murder. Someone gives you a harsh look, murder. Someone disrespects you, murder. Someone ruins your laundry, murder.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>Romance: WARNING, MILD SPOILERS</b><br /><br />and here we get into my .......... reservations. First of all, I just don't care that much about Jude and Cardan. Genuinely, I just care about the politics and characters and the romance is just kinda .. there. And while I admit I did enjoy their scenes because the two have good banter and presence when in the same scenes, I am SO iffy on their romance. <br /><br />The romance just ? Look, Cardan is literally awful. And Jude is just as awful back to him. And I could handle their romance when it was like "we hate eachother so much but also lets fuck" like it was some freak shit but I could handle it. and while it remains that, I also think it's slightly moving into "lets redeem the bad boy" territory and I'm .. not into it? First of all, it defeats the point of all the enemy lovers stuff but it's also just a bad trope. Anyways, when it was giving all that backstory about Cardan I was getting nervous. So I have my reservations. I will wait to see about Queen of Nothing. <br /><br />But also, I feel like I just don't care enough about them so I haven't really analysed or thought about it all that much? I know not caring about the romance is an unpopular opinion. ALTHO, I will say that scene where  they fuck while saying how much they hate eachother was hot. <br /><br /><i><blockquote>“You must be strong enough to strike and strike and strike again without tiring. The first lesson is to make yourself that strong.” <br /></blockquote></i><br /><br />Overall the Cruel Prince is a strong second book - definitely stronger than the first. It really develops on what was established in book one, but brings everything into a much larger scale, and raises the stakes so much. Jude is a great main character to follow, and I love how this series plays around with morality and virtue - I think the last book is going to be the best one of them all and I cannot wait for it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14685591615810448418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16103249299812073141">Once upon a time, there lived a girl named Roshani who was like "lol, lemme jus sit down with my coffee and read a Holly Black book." The girl had become one with the earth. Small thorns and blood-colored flowered bloomed around her head, and she choked out a single word: ". . . C A R D A N."<br/><br/>And that </span>
  <span id="freeText16103249299812073141" style="display:none">Once upon a time, there lived a girl named Roshani who was like "lol, lemme jus sit down with my coffee and read a Holly Black book." That was the end of that. The book consumed her. The coffee has long since evaporated and moss and ivy crawled over its porcelain shell and one could not tell it had ever been a drinking apparatus. C A R D A N."<br /><br />And that is why, my children, YOU DON'T READ A HOLLY BLACK BOOK KNOWING YOU'VE GOT BASICALLY TWO YEARS TO WAIT FOR THE FINALE. WTF. WHY DID I DO THIS TO MYSELF. <div id="review_2246189129" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2246189129" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2246189129?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=you-remind-me-of-the-babe">you-remind-me-of-the-babe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=faeries-and-elves">faeries-and-elves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2246189129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3966540006882860194"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>The relationship between author and reader is one of constant courting, and sequels are especially hard. You've won my trust once, with a stellar book, but that's no guarantee that I'm going to enjoy the sequel. Second Book Syndrome is totally a thing. It's what happens when authors get complacent and think that less effort can be expended when publishing their sequel. I <i>loved </i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2240784804' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE CRUEL PRINCE</a>, despite thinking it would be a disappointme</span>
  <span id="freeText3966540006882860194" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>The relationship between author and reader is one of constant courting, and sequels are especially hard. You've won my trust once, with a stellar book, but that's no guarantee that I'm going to enjoy the sequel. Second Book Syndrome is totally a thing. It's what happens when authors get complacent and think that less effort can be expended when publishing their sequel. I <i>loved </i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2240784804" rel="nofollow noopener">THE CRUEL PRINCE</a>, despite thinking it would be a disappointment, and immediately added THE WICKED KING to my to-read list. The wait was agonizing and plagued with self-doubt. Would I still enjoy the sequel as much as I'd enjoyed the prequel? Would it live up to my expectations? Did I <i>really </i>enjoy THE CRUEL PRINCE as much as I thought I had? The answer to all these questions was "yes." Yes, I enjoyed the sequel. Yes, it lived up to my expectations and then some. Yes, I love this series. It is the <i>bomb</i>.<br><br><br><br>THE WICKED KING starts off rather similarly to how THE CRUEL PRINCE did, by which I mean <i>slow AF</i>. Cardan is the High King of Faerie and also Jude's puppet, but her power over him only lasts for a year and a day, and she knows that as soon as that grace period is over, he's just going to be one person in a long line of many who wants Jude dead. Most of the first third of the book is Jude attempting to get all of her fey ducks in a row, scheming and conspiring, while also (hopelessly) trying to resist her growing attraction for Cardan.<br><br><br><br>I loved that THE WICKED KING was much more sensual and erotic than THE CRUEL PRINCE was. One of my biggest complaints about the first book was that it felt confined by the young adult genre, and the author wasn't really exploiting this world of treachery and sensuality to its full potential. This book really runs with those darker themes, and it does it in a way that feels adult without being smutty, if that makes sense. THE WICKED KING has all of the plotting and intrigue that makes <i>Game of Thrones </i>so popular, but does it without the exploitative gore and porn that also make the series feel cheap. I wish that more young adult books were like this, because Jude is a total antihero and completely unlike most helpless heroines I read about who dabble in perfection as if beauty and power are just essential oils you can soak up during your latest spa day. Jude has to scrabble and work for everything she's got, and she's so competent, you can't help but like her.<br><br><br><br>Also, the bad characters in this book are so awful that hating them is almost an art form. Locke reminds us right away why he's such a bastard, although he doesn't play as much of a role in this book as the previous one. Nicasia is that classic mean girl with anxiety that she tries so hard to hide. Taryn is a back-stabbing twat who likes to pretend that she's Jesus on the cross, and I was very proud of myself for not buying any of her very lame attempts at peace offerings, especially in light of the end of the novel. Fuck Taryn, seriously. Oh, and Cardan - the hero I love to hate and hate to love. The unresolved sexual tension between him and Jude is <i>amazing</i>. These are characters that I love to ship. I am the Helen of Troy of enemies-to-lovers in that I have launched a thousand ships for these sorts of relationships and <i>I regret nothing</i>. It really is like <i>Hana Yori Dango </i>meets <i>Game of Thrones</i>.<br><br><br><br>Best of all, we get to explore a new part of faerie land: the Undersea. Hence the crown slipping beneath the waves on the cover. Man, I love it when everything becomes clear as you read the book. Even the title makes sense once you find out more about Cardan and where he's coming from. The beginning is dull, but necessary because it ends up setting the stage for the hot mess of schemes upon schemes upon schemes that are peppered with sex, murder, violence, and intrigue in the last two acts of the book. And that ending is so cruel. I need <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032912-the-queen-of-nothing" rel="nofollow noopener">QUEEN OF NOTHING</a> in my hands <i>now</i>.<br><br><br><br>Why is 2020 so far away?<br><br><br><br>4.5 to 5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="3966540006882860194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
