<div id="review_2240448292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2240448292" />
    <a title="alana ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12402009-alana"><img alt="alana ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599221603p2/12402009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2240448292?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="alana ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="alana ♡" href="/user/show/12402009-alana">alana ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=reviewed-arcs">reviewed-arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2240448292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14473489554167302617">Can I just write an entire review repeating everything hurts, over and over again. Because <strong>EVERYTHING REALLY HURTS. </strong>It's been over a month since I've read this and it still just really, really fucking hurts, okay? Holly Black has done it again. She's ruined my life, made me question my sanity, and need a cold shower after reading this book. Even though I was incredibly excited for this book I still had my doubts that <em>The Wicked King </em>would top <em>The Cruel Prince. </em>I shouldn't have been worried thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText14473489554167302617" style="display:none">Can I just write an entire review repeating everything hurts, over and over again. Because <strong>EVERYTHING REALLY HURTS. </strong>It's been over a month since I've read this and it still just really, really fucking hurts, okay? Holly Black has done it again. She's ruined my life, made me question my sanity, and need a cold shower after reading this book. Even though I was incredibly excited for this book I still had my doubts that <em>The Wicked King </em>would top <em>The Cruel Prince. </em>I shouldn't have been worried though because this was everything. This book basically solidified the fact that I would indeed lay down my life for Jude and Cardan.<br /><br /><em>The Wicked King</em> has a lot more scheming and court politics in it compared to the first book, and while normally I'm more of an action packed type of gal, this really worked for me. I found myself falling more and more in love with my queen Jude and trying to figure Cardan out. Because I mean, as far as unpredictable characters go he is the most unpredictable, especially in the end 😭. The scheming, the twists and turns, the <strong>TENSION,</strong> was all unbelievably good. You will need a cold shower before, during, and after this book because the tension is so thick between Jude and Cardan it hurts. Also, here is a friendly reminder that Cardan had a tail, because I forgot and was shook to my core when his pants came off. You be the judge of why his pants came off, my lips are sealed...<br /><br />Anyway, less tail talk more book talk. We still have our amazing group of characters that we've grown to love and hate. Jude, is desperately trying to hold on to her power she tricked her way into. Cardan, is still defying Jude every step of the way. Taryn, is still The Worst Sister Alive. Locke, is awful. Madoc, is less than thrilled with the stunt Jude pulled in the end of the first book. Nicasia, is just as petty and spiteful as ever and ready for what her and her mother, the Queen of the Sea believe should be hers. So yeah, no pressure for Jude to hold on to her power over Cardan.<br /><br />Now, while I won't give away any of the plot twists or the ending, just know you are in for a world of pain. If you thought the ending of <em>The Cruel Prince </em>was torturous, oh sweet child, you haven't seen anything yet. What would this story be without twists and turns that physically make you feel like someone is squeezing you so tight you can't breathe? The ending of <em>The Cruel Prince</em> is laughable compared to the ending of <em>The Wicked King</em>. I would tell you all to prepare yourselves, but let's face it, no amount of preparation will have you ready. 2019 is going to be a year filled with<b> PAIN AND MISERY</b> until <em>The Queen of Nothing</em> is released in 2020.<br /><br /> <br /><br /><b>
  <strong>Favorite Quotes</strong>
</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Your ridiculous family might be surprised to find that not everything is solved by murder," Locke calls after me.<br /><br />"We would be surprised to find that," I call back.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>"Watching my back is the perfect opportunity to stick a knife in it."</em>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <em>"For a moment," he says, "I wondered if it wasn't you shooting bolts at me."</em>
  <br />
  <em>I make a face at him. "And what made you decide it wasn't?"</em>
  <br />
  <em>He grins up at me. "They missed."</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>"If you're the sickness, I suppose you can't also be the cure."</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>"We show her that I am no feckless High King."</em>
  <br />
  <em>"And how do we do that?" I ask.</em>
  <br />
  <em>"With great difficulty," he says.</em>
  <br />
  <em>"Since I fear she is right."</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />All in all, this book was perfect. It was the right amount of love, lust, hate, and pain. Now excuse me while I lay in bed and cry until 2020 because I have absolutely no idea how I'm going to live with myself until <em>The Queen of Nothing</em> is out!<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishchicksblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookishchick" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishchick_/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2350029471?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=2019-release">2019-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=gifted">gifted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=faves-ya-scifi-and-fantasy">faves-ya-scifi-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2350029471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8624521872783855811">When I went into this series I thought: <i>“tehehe, I bet this is over hyped”</i> — so believe me when I say I'm actually shocked by how much I've come to love this series. <br/><br/>It is not at all the kind of YA that I'm used to and neither are the characters. <i>The folk of the Air</i> is in a league of its own. <br/><br/>I loved every moment of this book. The scheming, the lies, the betrayals. *wipes away a tear* It was just so good. <br/><br/>⚠<b>
  <u>If you have not read book 1 (the cruel prince), do not go any further</u>
</b>⚠<br/><br/><br/><i>
  <b>Power is much</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText8624521872783855811" style="display:none">When I went into this series I thought: <i>“tehehe, I bet this is over hyped”</i> — so believe me when I say I'm actually shocked by how much I've come to love this series. <br /><br />It is not at all the kind of YA that I'm used to and neither are the characters. <i>The folk of the Air</i> is in a league of its own. <br /><br />I loved every moment of this book. The scheming, the lies, the betrayals. *wipes away a tear* It was just so good. <br /><br />⚠<b>
  <u>If you have not read book 1 (the cruel prince), do not go any further</u>
</b>⚠<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>Power is much easier to acquire than it is to hold on to.</b>
</i><br /><br />Jude is finally where she always dreamt of being – in power. But keeping it is more difficult than gaining it. Her reasons for her actions leading up to where she is now, is to make sure Oak is safe. <br /><br />Her bargain with Carden means she is only in control for one year and a day. But she likes being in charge even if none of the faeries know that Jude is the brains behind Carden, the one pulling the strings. <br /><br />Time is running out. Enemies and traitors are everywhere. And Carden, who is still pissed about being tricked into being king, is starting to look too comfortable on the throne. Jude has to figure out a way to make sure he doesn't get rid of her at his first chance. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Fear is terrible, but the combination of hope and fear is worse.</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />This series is not for everyone. I can see why many are not a fan of Jude and her selfish ambition. There is also the ‘problem’ of the first half of the books dragging but I find myself NOT MINDING ONE BIT. <br /><br />I've come to notice that Holly has a trend in having a slow pace for the first half of her books. It makes me excited to get to the second half where <b>I know she will shock my socks off.</b><br /><br />Jude is so lonely in this book. She has all these secrets and responsibilities and no one to share them with. I was so proud of her for all that she accomplished.<br /><br />I was not Carden's biggest fan in book 1, but I actually have come to really like him. Jude and the Court really underestimate him. They think he's this spoiled brat who couldn't care less about what's going on, but I think Carden is smart and knows how to play a part. For those of you who read the book, you know what I'm talking about 😏.<br /><br />I know that many readers are outraged at <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Carden for what he does at the end. But to be honest my first thought was: <i>GO CARDEN!</i> <br /><br />I mean it was pretty clever of him. He ain't nobodies puppet now 😏. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The plot twists were superb and the ending was shocking and brilliant. There are so many possibilities for how the final book will end and I'm so nervous but excited!!<br /><br />______<br /><u>
  <b>My reviews for:</b>
</u><br />NB: <i>all these books are set in the same world.</i><br /><br /><i>Modern Faerie Tales series</i><br />Book #1 : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2597323817" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe</a><br />Book #2 : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606793925" rel="nofollow noopener">Valiant</a><br />Book #3 : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606793968" rel="nofollow noopener">Ironside</a><br /><br /><i>The Folk of the Air series</i><br />Book #1 : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2417729031" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince</a><br />Book #1.5 : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2451767982" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Sisters</a><br />Book #3 : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2350029537" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Nothing</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11359476762752319355">I do not know what is becoming of me.<br/><br/>I have a 2.94 average rating. (Before you ask - yes, my heart is made of ice and pain and suffering and knives.)   <span id="freeText11359476762752319355" style="display:none">I do not know what is becoming of me.<br /><br />I have a 2.94 average rating. (Before you ask - yes, my heart is made of ice and pain and suffering and knives.) I so frequently have unpopular opinions that I made a shelf for them (so they can band together in their unpopularity and become friends). I eat YA bestsellers for breakfast.<br /><br />I didn’t even like the first book in this series!<br /><br />And yet...I kind of enjoyed reading this book?!<br /><br />I didn’t even mean to ever pick it up!<br /><br />If you put me in a library and tell me said library is closing in 45 minutes and also that after that it will be closed for at least two weeks (but really for the foreseeable future), things happen.<br /><br />I may, for example, pick up the sequel to a book I did not like, for some reason operating under the belief that I had intended to read it. <br /><br />Apparently, my reward for such stressful experiences is CONFUSION.<br /><br />I can’t even put into words why I didn’t hate this.<br /><br />I mean, I hate these characters. <br /><br />Jude is annoying (I did not care for Feyre at all, and while she is not Feyre levels of nightmare material, she does belong to the same Vaguely Badass With Very Few Other Traits character family). <br /><br />Cardan is just...simply the It’s Okay That I’m An Asshole Because I Have A Tragic Past trope, dialed allll the way up to abusive.<br /><br />Throw them together into a toxic yucky will-they-won’t-they romance and you should have a fail-proof recipe to make me hate a book.<br /><br />AND YET!!!<br /><br />Plus there were a million tiny little annoying things of the variety that tend to warrant a whole page in a seven-page rant review.<br /><br />Like any of the emotional reactions of any character, none of which make sense.<br /><br />Or so many of the things Jude does. Jude’s actions are nonsense to me. The girl wears a mask of her own face to a masquerade where she’s supposed to be disguised? She says she can’t think of the words to command Cardan when literally “I command you to ____” would do the trick? She’s a full-on idiot at some points and a war-planning master of strategy at others?<br /><br />I don’t get it.<br /><br />But, at the same time…I had so much fun reading this????<br /><br />At a certain point, I was like “I should get back to reading The Wicked King. I wonder why I’m so into reading it? It’s not like I like it....oh wait holy sh*t oh my god I like it. I’m ruined. My reputation is in shambles. I will be mocked in the side streets and back alleys of the online book community.”<br /><br />But even worse, that cliffhanger at the end...I didn’t even intend to read this book and then suddenly all I can think about is finishing the series????<br /><br />What is HAPPENING to me.<br /><br />Bottom line: A book so fun it’ll cause an identity crisis.<br /><br />That’s the Emma Guarantee (™).<br /><br />----------<br /><br />so, to recap:<br />- i hate these characters<br />- i'm not a fan of the writing <br />- many parts of this mad me roll my eyes<br /><br />but...somehow...<br /><br />i enjoyed reading it????<br /><br />WHAT IS HAPPENING TO ME.<br /><br />review to come / 3 stars<br /><br />----------<br /><br />yes, i am reading this book.<br /><br />no, i did not like The Cruel Prince.<br /><br />we exist</span>
  <a data-text-id="11359476762752319355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ncpPxMnVIraacopaCIEk3RWYEze1jkcPe5l8AvjXQsgN1pLyRg2txVsXifczXTEEQ3Fh+znMrWRkq1i6CeyQnA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KCKSjfLgjk35cntnMLjS7km2W2KqiISgda147nyTFD24Pk+7fTgBPjgXeMoLZMc3H18pribKbstqn1xWjajGaQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer7221743668998547965">Holly Black is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of over thirty fantasy novels for kids and teens. She has been a finalist for an Eisner Award and the Lodestar Award, and the recipient of the Mythopoeic Award, a Nebula, and a Newbery Honor. Her books have been translated into 32 languages worldwide and adapted for film. She currently lives in New England with her husband and son in a house </span>
  <span id="freeText7221743668998547965" style="display:none">Holly Black is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of over thirty fantasy novels for kids and teens. She has been a finalist for an Eisner Award and the Lodestar Award, and the recipient of the Mythopoeic Award, a Nebula, and a Newbery Honor. Her books have been translated into 32 languages worldwide and adapted for film. She currently lives in New England with her husband and son in a house with a secret library.</span>
